  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_abf901bd-bc42-402d-90c1-1079b8bb320f'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer15460969645658034312"><br/><div><b>The International Bestseller</b><br/><br/>For Thom Kindred, life is nothing spectacular.   <span id="freeText15460969645658034312" style="display:none"><br /><div><b>The International Bestseller</b><br /><br />For Thom Kindred, life is nothing spectacular. A stroke victim, Thom finds himself partially incapacitated and battling daily to regain control of his life. Moved by haunting dreams of his youth, he travels back to the wooded land where he grew up to recuperate. Surrounded by the comforts of Castle Bracken, Thom plans to relive old, forgotten memories.<br /><br />But Thom's return has stirred an ancient evil at Castle Bracken, one cloaked in the guise of a friend. His only chance for survival lies in a world that he no longer believes in. <br /><br />International bestselling author James Herbert opens the door into a place of wonder and terrible danger; where the unexpected becomes the norm, where the separation of dreams and nightmares is thin, and where "Once upon a time . . ." doesn't always lead to a happy ending. <br /></div><br /></span>

<div id="review_892848318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/892848318" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/892848318?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jared Fogle and Jada Fire</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer892848318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8187472262171693193">Boy oh boy, this book is shit. Fortunately, it was a buddy read with my good friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32669562-thomas-str-mquist' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thomas Strömquist</a> so I didn't have to suffer alone. Funnily enough, I asked Thomas if we could skip the book we'd initially agreed to read this month, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16278152-the-venus-complex?ac=1&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Venus Complex</a>, because I wasn't in the mood for erotic horror. Thomas had also mentioned wanting to read some James Herbert. I decided on this book. Why, yes, Virginia, I am a fucking moron.<br/><br/>I was under the impression that James Herbert was a horror author, that</span>
  <span id="freeText8187472262171693193" style="display:none">Boy oh boy, this book is shit. Fortunately, it was a buddy read with my good friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32669562-thomas-str-mquist" rel="nofollow noopener">Thomas Strömquist</a> so I didn't have to suffer alone. Funnily enough, I asked Thomas if we could skip the book we'd initially agreed to read this month, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16278152-the-venus-complex?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">The Venus Complex</a>, because I wasn't in the mood for erotic horror. Thomas had also mentioned wanting to read some James Herbert. I decided on this book. Why, yes, Virginia, I am a fucking moron.<br /><br />I was under the impression that James Herbert was a horror author, that the man was known for his scary books involving rats and fog and other such horror-trope-y shit. If <i>Once...</i> is any taste of his horror chops, I feel comfortable saying, I've read more terrifying Dr. Seuss books. I was in the mood for some gothic horror and I got a fairytale full of cliches and horrible, and I mean fucking atrocious, writing. I was expecting evil imps and I got loads of porn that seemingly was written by a man-child. I don't mind sex in my horror novels. I don't even mind blood and guts mixed with graphically-detailed sex. What I don't like reading about is actual porn. If I wanted porn, I'd watch porn. If I wanted to read porn, I'd hit up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar" rel="nofollow noopener">Kells</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelbs</a> for some for-science recommendations. Here, lemme give you a list of the various sexual experiences found within these pages:<br /><br />A man stumbles across a little girl masturbating in the woods and becomes aroused. If you're asking, "What the fuck?" you damn well should be. Our hero Thom first assumes that this undine (human-sized fairy) is a child, but even though she looks ten, she still manages to give old Thom a raging fuck rod. Somehow I'm supposed to be cool with a grown-ass man being aroused by a masturbating child? Fuck this guy. Goddamn pedo. But wait! It's cool because she's not really a child! Oh, oh, oh! Thank fucking Tom Cruise... But wait... Thom didn't know she wasn't a child when his meat-javelin reached full stroke potential. So, yeah, still, fuck this guy. <br /><br />Then we have a succubus sucking Thom's dinker and absconding with his man-varnish. Little demon fucker literally steals Thom's dry-walling batter and runs off. Cue chase scene wherein Thom tries to recover his dick yogurt. This scene is goddamn hilarious but is written in such a way as to be taken seriously. Fuck you, Author Man.<br /><br />Then we have a lesbian seduction scene involving a witch and Thom's physical therapist. There is some inner thought from the PT gal that goes something to the tune of, "I'm not a lesbian. But there was that one time in college..." HAHAHAHAHA!!! Fuck you, Book! I've heard that exact line in actual lesbian porn. For real. Yes, I have no shame. I've watched many a porno, and I know for a fact that such dialogue exists. It's even a bad joke amongst my peers. "I don't do that, but there was this one time in college..." Eat a dick, Herbert.<br /><br />Now we come (get it? "come" wink, wink, nod, nod) to Thom and the undine fucking for the first time. This is where all the "inner juices" repetition started. Those two words are used over and over again, time after time, to describe both his and her fluids. There's even a point where the author says that Thom "felt his own wetness". Now, I understand Herbert meant Thom had some pre-drip going on, but that shit just sounds weird. I swear to Pickleberry Jesus, if I read the word "juices" again in a sexual context I'm going to torch whatever book I'm reading. That word is now off limits. Just like "moist". And then, when dude fills up her cone with a load of his vanilla soft serve, he sees Heaven and the very moment all of creation came to be. <br /><br />*bangs head in car door then stumbles back to the keyboard to finish review*<br /><br />Then we have a boring BJ as done by the aforementioned witch to appease the guy she's scheming with. Whatever. The blowjob is one of those "Only if I must" kinda things. Nothing even remotely titillating about it. Why is it there? Because Herbert had gone five pages without talking about sex so he needed to rectify the issue.<br /><br />Finally, the book ends with more porn, as in, the final fucking scene is a final fucking scene. And yes, <b>SPOILERS</b>, but I don't care enough to hide them. <br /><br />Thom has to fuck the undine backwards in time, as if his dick is a goddamn De Lorean going 88mph. What. The actual. Fuck? I've heard of figuratively fucking someone into the next century, but this shit is literal. He literally fucks her into the past. And that's it. That's the end. After he busts his time-travelling nut, he strolls off into the goddamn horizon like the porno version of Rhett Butler.<br /><br />There is one good scene in this entire novel and it involves spiders. That shit was gross and unsettling and squishy and BAH! Creeped me the fuck out. But that's one scene in 460 pages. <br /><br />In summation: The entire plot is thin to the point of being nonexistent. The sex is forced and horribly written. The writing is plagued by repetition, and I honestly haven't a clue how this man became so popular. I hate to speak ill of the dead, but it's not like Herbert's gonna care, because... well, because he's this side of rotten at this point. I hope he's getting that good-good from Satan. <br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: Fairy porn.</b><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8187472262171693193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1633006926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1633006926" />
    <a title="Thomas Strömquist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32669562-thomas-str-mquist"><img alt="Thomas Strömquist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590007844p2/32669562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1633006926?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Strömquist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Strömquist" href="/user/show/32669562-thomas-str-mquist">Thomas Strömquist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780330469043" href="/book/show/17080139-once">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1633006926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17470195600295614482">Oh gosh, where to start? I'll admit to being entranced by the narrative for the first third of this and I really liked it that far! Therefore, I so much wanted to put something more that a measly one-star for the book. Until I remembered that the two-star rating on Goodreads is defined as "it was ok". Which made the one star rating a so-called "no-brainer". Following the (admittedly) well-written and alluring intro this thing descended into a cesspool of fairy-tale clichés and tasteless porn. My</span>
  <span id="freeText17470195600295614482" style="display:none">Oh gosh, where to start? I'll admit to being entranced by the narrative for the first third of this and I really liked it that far! Therefore, I so much wanted to put something more that a measly one-star for the book. Until I remembered that the two-star rating on Goodreads is defined as "it was ok". Which made the one star rating a so-called "no-brainer". Following the (admittedly) well-written and alluring intro this thing descended into a cesspool of fairy-tale clichés and tasteless porn. My initial fantasy of finding another read-worthy 80's and 90's horror novelist turned to ashes in a few chapters... <br /><br />The rest of this review will contain some kind of SPOILERS, so if you are serious about reading this book with no prejudice, I suggest you turn to my great buddy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5751572.Edward_Lorn" title="Edward Lorn" rel="nofollow noopener">Edward Lorn</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/892848318" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> instead. Not that he hid his spoilers either, but his review will bring much more entertainment and literary value than this book, <i>and</i> it may persuade you to give it a miss!<br /><br />Following the good (if not very fast moving) first third or so, we are treated to some odd sexual tension scenes, that seem mostly awkward. After that, we plunge head-first into a impossibly long part where we're bounced between a lesbian lovemaking scene that seems very strange (I'm no expert here, but I did study anatomy and physiology, and I don't think that is how it works or should be done). And I do think the script writers of "Orange is the New Black" went: "nailed it!" instead of hanging their heads in shame like they probably always should... Where was I? Oh right, bounced between that and <i>a fairytale</i>. <br /><br />Now, I never found a fairytale story in an adult book that actually holds up...and this is no exception. There are fairies (and witches and goblins and gnomes and whatever) - children know about them, but forget as they get older. Humans don't sense them, since they are relying on what they can see and prove and not (as they should) crap that is totally improbable, unverifiable and without logical reason to believe in. We know better. The elfish world is far more advanced and better and finer and prettier and way more powerful than the human world. But the human way of life smothers the other world because reasons. And if you thought you could fix that, you can't, because reasons. And rules. And magic. <br /><br />Still here then? Well, after the ping-pong of explicit male-oriented lesbian porn &lt;-&gt; silly fairytale finally grows old, the author ups the ante by switching the first story line first to some sort of S&amp;M abusive lesbian porn and then pure assault (with sexual overtones), while the fairy-tale part turns to fairy porn. The fairy porn is strange, because it manages to be both explicit porn and (since we suffered a big helping of insta-love) "hearts beating as one" and the cheesy like. <br /><br />Apart from that, the writing and editing gets continuously sloppier (so much that I started to doubt the same author penned the first part). Page 52: <i>"- but there had always been something about spiders that had turned [Thom's] legs to jelly and sent his heart racing"</i>. Page 335: <i>"It wasn't as if Thom had ever been afraid of spiders or any other..."</i>. Oh, and the spider invasion? The guy's house <i>fills</i> up with spiders - kind of scary imagery at first - after what feels like a hundred pages - not so much. You know how you find out the number of spiders? You count the legs and divide by eight. You'll have plenty of time! And then it happens again, I can't...<br /><br />Two more (just in case anybody is still reading): during the dramatic climatic events, a mortally wounded man refuses to relax, but must tell what's on his mind: <i>"Do you know what kind?"</i> *incredibly dramatic music* (in my head, that is) <i>"Can you...can you guess?</i> *Curtain*<br /><br />Last one (promise!) <i>"...that was the moment when something else happened. Something </i>extraordinary<i>"</i>. Because all the other turning worst fears into physical manifestations, fairies, gnomes, goblins, murder, betrayal and stuff is just same old, same old.<br /><br />No, I won't even go into the ending. Rest assured it did <b>not</b> redeem anything.<br /><br />What I will remember most about this book is the "battle for his semen" and the authors obsession with body fluids and their movement in general - and, oh, of course the one with pubic hair (the absence, that is). This is not a happy conclusion. But, I will also remember that I greatly enjoyed reading it with Edward (which is always a special treat, no matter the story) and the marvelous (if a tad smug) support from friends - foremost <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelby</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelly</a> - we are waiting for your s̶a̶c̶r̶i̶f̶i̶c̶e̶ reviews!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17470195600295614482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_794554442" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794554442" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/794554442?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=repetitive">repetitive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=bought-from-bandit">bought-from-bandit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=got-in-2013">got-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794554442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2834912018981917458"><br/>Once is an adult fairy-tale fantasy with bizarre sexual scenarios, a nostalgic touch, and gothic feel. There’s a whole bunch going into this one. The front of the book has stunning artwork for several pages too, and the author clearly had fun breaking up the classic “Once upon a time” line between pages, instead starting chapter one with “death.” This is one of those books where you get the bigger impact reading the beginning in book form rather than electronic.<br/><br/>The length is drawn out considerin</span>
  <span id="freeText2834912018981917458" style="display:none"><br />Once is an adult fairy-tale fantasy with bizarre sexual scenarios, a nostalgic touch, and gothic feel. There’s a whole bunch going into this one. The front of the book has stunning artwork for several pages too, and the author clearly had fun breaking up the classic “Once upon a time” line between pages, instead starting chapter one with “death.” This is one of those books where you get the bigger impact reading the beginning in book form rather than electronic.<br /><br />The length is drawn out considering the storyline, which doesn’t hold enough scenes and action to justify page count. The writing style is beautifully done, complimenting the nostalgic and fantasy feel of the protagonist. I do wish less reflection had taken place, where a shorter length would have minimized the ‘dragging on’, spicing it up a bit.<br /><br />Character wise, Thom is likeable with realistic dimensional, coming back home after a serious health setback. Hugo interested me because of his dysfunctional weaknesses and the villain turned out satisfyingly monstrous. I do wish more time had been spent about the grandfather. The elves and creatures in the forest were fantastical and intriguing, bringing the fairy tale element to life full force, and I liked the revelations Thom learned about himself and what the future holds for the land. <br /><br />Sexual scenes are surreal and fit perfectly into the story, especially the erotic scene where he first encounters a main character. It shifts to another disturbing sequence that I won’t spoil here, but let’s just say that one ended up icky. There’s a few more sex scenes, including two characters you wouldn’t suspect, taking up nearly an entire chapter in length.<br /><br />Overall the premise is good but there’s too much fluff to avoid getting bored sometimes. Characters are worthy of reading about, but you can only care so long in between something happening and characters ‘explaining things.’ The finale, with its flashy battle, worked. Pacing is too slow, but the atmosphere is rich and enshrouded with gothic fantasy. I expected more, perhaps some slimming down would have helped it, but it’s a decent book that stands out as unique.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2834912018981917458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_502965326" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/502965326" />
    <a title="Sam Fleming" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5005399-sam-fleming"><img alt="Sam Fleming" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442656859p2/5005399.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/502965326?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Fleming" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Fleming" href="/user/show/5005399-sam-fleming">Sam Fleming</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer502965326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5811959049925396836">The problem with Herbert is, to my mind, that he has always tended more towards slasher-fic than true horror. Oh, and the porn. Dear gods. The porn. I mean, I liked him when I was a teenager and still thought that Iron Maiden’s Eddie was just the coolest thing ever, but as I grew older I came to realise that a chainsaw-wielding maniac and some explicit passages about blow jobs do not a horrifying story make.<br/><br/><i>Once</i> declared itself to be a fairy story, of sorts. I don’t know how it came to be on my </span>
  <span id="freeText5811959049925396836" style="display:none">The problem with Herbert is, to my mind, that he has always tended more towards slasher-fic than true horror. Oh, and the porn. Dear gods. The porn. I mean, I liked him when I was a teenager and still thought that Iron Maiden’s Eddie was just the coolest thing ever, but as I grew older I came to realise that a chainsaw-wielding maniac and some explicit passages about blow jobs do not a horrifying story make.<br /><br /><i>Once</i> declared itself to be a fairy story, of sorts. I don’t know how it came to be on my shelf, but I knew I hadn’t read it, so I thought what the hell.<br /><br />Either it was ghost-written or my inner grammar goblin has grown hungrier as I've aged. Spelling mistakes. Grammar mistakes. Punctuation mistakes. Quotation marks missing in the strangest places. It was almost as if it had been written by Stewie from <i>Family Guy</i> with occasional help from Quagmire.<br /><br />Language issues aside, I’m sure that the explicit sex in Herbert’s earlier work wasn’t so, well, gratuitous. I don’t need 4 pages of our hero watching an undine masturbate. Really. Nor do I need almost an entire chapter describing how TEH EEEEBIL WITCH (called a "Wicca" in this, which I’m sure will delight all the Gardnerians in the audience) conducts lesbian drug rape on the physiotherapist [explicit example redacted].<br /><br />No, no, and no. And, lest we forget, the entire plot resolves around the Messiah trope, played absolutely straight and by the numbers. Right down to being loved by the birds and bees, and dear gods, he’s a carpenter! If that weren’t enough, it’s explicitly stated that he is just like Jesus.<br /><br />The prose is shoddy, the story tedious, the pseudo-philosophical ramblings risible. To put it simply, this is one of those books that acts as discouragement to the aspiring writer, because you realise that the only way you’ll ever be a bestselling author is to produce absolute dreck.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5811959049925396836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021124762" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24405408-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600655146p2/24405408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021124762?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/24405408-dawn">Dawn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021124762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer664393657430000625">I adored this! I listened to it on Audible, so it took quite some time for me, but it was so very good. I must say I have not read anything like this from James Herbert. It was not the typical horror I am accustomed to, it is really a fantasy book with lots of fairies, witches and the like. It is also very sensual, which I was not expecting either! Totally worth the time if you get to read it. I recommend it for sure, it was a breath of fresh air and as always I love his writing style.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_119704955" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119704955" />
    <a title="Peter Chandler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4223368-peter-chandler"><img alt="Peter Chandler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1283179608p2/4223368.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119704955?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter Chandler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter Chandler" href="/user/show/4223368-peter-chandler">Peter Chandler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119704955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15127603478313373804">It is impossible to shake the inescapable sense that this book must be labouring under some sort of Glamour. Certainly all is very stylish upon the surface, a great deal of artistry has gone into the cover, its map and it's imagery and yet none of this can hide the gaping empty void where the actual story should be. There are so many things that are bad about this book it's hard to choose where to start but I will begin by mentioning the general prose style and its habit of indulging in unnecess</span>
  <span id="freeText15127603478313373804" style="display:none">It is impossible to shake the inescapable sense that this book must be labouring under some sort of Glamour. Certainly all is very stylish upon the surface, a great deal of artistry has gone into the cover, its map and it's imagery and yet none of this can hide the gaping empty void where the actual story should be. There are so many things that are bad about this book it's hard to choose where to start but I will begin by mentioning the general prose style and its habit of indulging in unnecessarily long sentences, with lots of commas and subclauses - of the kind that contain the most banal and obvious observations that are supposed to pass of insight - and at times render the story confusingly unreadable. Much like that.<br /><br />I've not read James Herbert before, but I understand this book had been an effort to branch out from the more usual fare of horror and chills into something broader and deeper. Sadly though endless meandering sentences does no more equal deep insights than awkwardly written sex equals expressions of human desires whilst a man meeting a bunch of fairies and wondering a bit whether it could be real is no kind of investigation into the nature of belief. Perhaps ironically the only brief moment when I found the book did come to life was at one of the moments of straight horror featuring a bottomless jar of spiders. The rest of the time the tale remains resolutely lifeless, rendering almost comical its apparent pretensions to some deeper insights or truth. <br /><br />Then there is the plot which, when it does happen to come along in the last quarter of the book is of such dreadfully contrived and melodramatic proportions as might come out of some bad soap-opera. There is also the characterisation, or perhaps that should be absence of characterisation. This point is most particularly egregious when it comes to the actions of the women. At no point is any attempt made to explain the origins of this book's female antagonist and scarce little mention of what lies behind the actions of any of the others. All this renders then a somewhat unpleasantly stereotypical characterisation of women, either devious and manipulative in the use of their sex or otherwise pure and innocent and beautiful when it suits this decidedly male fantasy for them to be. Were the male hero so very dense, yet occasionally inexplicably insightful, I might yet be somewhat more angry about it.<br /><br />Yet the aspect of this book that threatens to invoke my wrath even more can be neatly summed up by the two points in the narrative when our ill-defined hero is actually compared to the figure of Jesus! The sheer breathtaking arrogance of this empty little book is truly awe inspiring. I'm an atheist and still it makes me angry, or would at least, were it not quite so laughable. I have wondered at times whether I have been too hard in my evaluation of an innocent and playful fantasy of witches and fairies and elves and then I remember no, you actually thought your hero worthy of comparison to Jesus! It's ridiclous, if not hilarious, not to mention pretentious, arrogant, tawdry, empty (not to mention the confusingly rambling prose), with a somewhat unpleasant air of female objectivity and overall just bad. <br /><br />Really, very bad indeed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15127603478313373804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_605980231" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605980231" />
    <a title="Jean-Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2972015-jean-paul"><img alt="Jean-Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288749246p2/2972015.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/605980231?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean-Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean-Paul" href="/user/show/2972015-jean-paul">Jean-Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605980231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14407421973672961184">James Herbert Once...<br/><br/><br/>I don't often get the opportunity to review a book which I really didn't like. At least not since college and assigned reading lists. I'm not beholden to others to do my reviews so I generally try to pick books which I think I'll like and I can stop reading if I don't like it. Mostly though I do finish books once I start them and even on books that star off rocky I usually find something redeeming in their pages.<br/>And then we have "Once..." by James Herbert. I think it's usual</span>
  <span id="freeText14407421973672961184" style="display:none">James Herbert Once...<br /><br /><br />I don't often get the opportunity to review a book which I really didn't like. At least not since college and assigned reading lists. I'm not beholden to others to do my reviews so I generally try to pick books which I think I'll like and I can stop reading if I don't like it. Mostly though I do finish books once I start them and even on books that star off rocky I usually find something redeeming in their pages.<br />And then we have "Once..." by James Herbert. I think it's usually a bad sign if ellipsis is part of the book title... The cover looks promising, silver fairies and foxes in entwined with thorny vines in front of what appears to be a castle and the words "The International Bestseller" emblazoned in red across the top. Looks like a nice fantasy paper-back. What could go wrong?<br />I could easily go into rant mode, but I want to keep this review short as I really do not want to devote any more of my time to thinking about this book than I already have while reading it. Mr. Herbert's grasp of the fantastic is akin to a day laborers grasp of Spackle. He's seen it, he's touched it, he can probably put up something that looks like it if you give him time and the tools, but in the end it won't pass the test of time and it's a poor veneer on a hole.<br />To say I was disappointed with the prose of this book is to put it lightly. The descriptions of fairies, gnomes, elves, and fantastical beasts that populate the periphery of the magical forest our protagonist stumbles through are so mundane and matter of fact that any sense of wonder I might have possessed was wrung out of me like a damp dish rag.<br />I haven't even touched on the plot, because there isn't much of one. Your generic orphan boy grows up with a mysterious past and comes back to the home he left and the vague memories of magic that he had long denied. You know the trope... what he might be the heir to the fortune? What he might be party fairy himself? You don't say... skip past the completely disappointing evil witch/bitch villainess and fast forward to the completely pulled out of nowhere SPOILER (TIME TRAVEL) Dues Ex Machina and put a bow on it. This thing is ... done.<br />Not recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14407421973672961184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1298596521?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Brian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Brian" href="/user/show/16112063-david-brian">David Brian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10018156860339012069">I grew up reading James Herbert, and I honestly consider myself a fan of his writing. This was disappointing.<br/>Firstly, this isn't actually a horror story. This in itself was not the problem as Mr. Herbert has previously turned his hand from the horror genre, with the excellent Fluke being a prime example of this.<br/>The book is actually a fairy tale for the modern age. Following his recovery from a serious stroke, the irritatingly named Thom Kindred returns to his ancestral home within the grounds of</span>
  <span id="freeText10018156860339012069" style="display:none">I grew up reading James Herbert, and I honestly consider myself a fan of his writing. This was disappointing.<br />Firstly, this isn't actually a horror story. This in itself was not the problem as Mr. Herbert has previously turned his hand from the horror genre, with the excellent Fluke being a prime example of this.<br />The book is actually a fairy tale for the modern age. Following his recovery from a serious stroke, the irritatingly named Thom Kindred returns to his ancestral home within the grounds of Castle Bracken. Thom hopes to reconnect with old friends and forgotten memories. He does this, but it comes with a cost.<br />Thom soon discovers that fairies are real, and so too are other, darker things.<br />This wasn't a terrible book, but it was padded with far too much descriptive prose, and the sex scenes... my God, the sex scenes. I'm not in any way opposed to people getting their rocks off in literature, but this was littered with such scenes; it began to feel as though they were there purely as further padding.<br />Also, the wicked witch of the piece is continually refereed to as a wiccan. A strange word choice for the antagonist.<br />Overall, not a bad book, but not a great one either. I'd recommend James Herbert to anyone who enjoys horror, but I'd advise giving this one a miss.</span>

<div id="review_38303586" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38303586" />
    <a title="Kenci" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1738265-kenci"><img alt="Kenci" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516373236p2/1738265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38303586?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenci" href="/user/show/1738265-kenci">Kenci</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765302854" href="/book/show/1409662.Once">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1738265-kenci?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1738265-kenci?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38303586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer411526089583765308"><b>Once</b> by James Herbert was more than a little disappointing. Yes, I had read other reviews first and they were all pretty consistent about this book... sucking. Yet I still hoped for more. The synopsis sounded great and I really liked James Herbert's <b>Haunted</b>. And from the synopsis, I was hoping for something more like John Connolly's <b>The Book of Lost Things</b> or Neil Gaiman's <b>Stardust</b>. Faery with some horror elements. My expectations were set way too high.<br/><br/>The story initially drew me in and had me q</span>
  <span id="freeText411526089583765308" style="display:none"><b>Once</b> by James Herbert was more than a little disappointing. Yes, I had read other reviews first and they were all pretty consistent about this book... sucking. Yet I still hoped for more. The synopsis sounded great and I really liked James Herbert's <b>Haunted</b>. And from the synopsis, I was hoping for something more like John Connolly's <b>The Book of Lost Things</b> or Neil Gaiman's <b>Stardust</b>. Faery with some horror elements. My expectations were set way too high.<br /><br />The story initially drew me in and had me quickly turning the pages, but it wasn't long before the descriptions of Faery became tedious rather than magical. The horror was gross rather than creepy. But I think what irritated me the most and put me off was the unnecessary sex that did absolutely nothing to further the plot. 300 pages in and I no longer cared about any of the characters; who lived or who died.<br /><br />So, if you are looking for some great dark fantasy and adult fairy tales, skip this one and read instead John Connolly's <b>The Book of Lost Things</b>, Neil Gaiman's <b>Stardust</b>, Lord Dunsany's <b>The King of Elfland's Daughter</b>, or any of the fairy tale collections edited by Ellen Datlow and Terri Windling. Just to name a few...<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="411526089583765308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10770310721854409237">This James Herbert novel is very different to many of his others and introduces us to Thom Kindred who after a serious accident returns to his childhood home of Little Bracken set deep in the mysterious forest surrounding the stately home of Castle Bracken. <br/><br/>The narrative sets up quite a spooky feeling about the setting and also the both houses. The Characters of Hugo Bleeth and Nell Quick are not who they seem and then we find out that the forest is populated by a whole host of incredible mythic</span>
  <span id="freeText10770310721854409237" style="display:none">This James Herbert novel is very different to many of his others and introduces us to Thom Kindred who after a serious accident returns to his childhood home of Little Bracken set deep in the mysterious forest surrounding the stately home of Castle Bracken. <br /><br />The narrative sets up quite a spooky feeling about the setting and also the both houses. The Characters of Hugo Bleeth and Nell Quick are not who they seem and then we find out that the forest is populated by a whole host of incredible mythical animals and elves and wicked evil creatures from our nightmares and fairy tales that interact with Thom. <br /><br />The story is very original and sometimes erotic, sometimes menacing; I wouldn't exactly call it Horror, more a good old fashioned haunted love story. Very good none the less. </span>

<div id="review_523725536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/523725536" />
    <a title="Stargazer85" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17046445-stargazer85"><img alt="Stargazer85" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a title="Stargazer85" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stargazer85" href="/user/show/17046445-stargazer85">Stargazer85</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer523725536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15091450839231600770">This is probably one of my most favourite books to date. Dark fantasy based on faery folk with the approach that not all fairytales are pink and fluffy as it were. For any adult that appreciates the idea that fairytales never started off as princesses in castles but more on open lustful desires, then this is definitely worth a read!</span>

<div id="review_127097793" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127097793" />
    <a title="Greg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/361125-greg"><img alt="Greg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506683246p2/361125.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127097793?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg" href="/user/show/361125-greg">Greg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330376136" href="/book/show/1045756.Once">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/361125-greg?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127097793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16323911571047223806">This was an entertaining dark fantasy with a fair bit of sex thrown into it! The plot is straight forward enough with few real surprises - it’s typical good versus evil fare – so some people might be disappointed if they wanted something to tax their brains a little! <br/><br/>There was, however, an interesting overview of the Lloyds of London insurance scandal of the 1980s on pp. 134-6. This is rather topical given the current global financial problems caused by (among other things) the collapse of the s</span>
  <span id="freeText16323911571047223806" style="display:none">This was an entertaining dark fantasy with a fair bit of sex thrown into it! The plot is straight forward enough with few real surprises - it’s typical good versus evil fare – so some people might be disappointed if they wanted something to tax their brains a little! <br /><br />There was, however, an interesting overview of the Lloyds of London insurance scandal of the 1980s on pp. 134-6. This is rather topical given the current global financial problems caused by (among other things) the collapse of the sub-prime market in the US; financial deregulation (or at least the non-enforcement of existing regulations); widespread over-reliance on credit by a public lured into increasing indebtedness by the banks and credit card companies; and governments’ (mis)use of taxpayers’ money to solve the banking crisis. I wonder what horror or fantasy novels will come to be set in the current day (or its aftermath) with the ongoing financial problems as a backdrop?<br /><br />There was also some humour in this novel – I particularly liked the suggestion that a certain popular singer belonged to a type of fairy folk on p. 268, although whether she would like it too is another thing.<br /><br />Before the advent of the mobile phone, it was possible for people to find themselves in difficult situations – whether out in the wilderness or close to human settlement – with no way of communicating to anybody for help. Nowadays, many people are just a phone call away from help, as their phone is never far from their hand/pocket/handbag. In <i>Once…</i>, the protagonist has a mobile phone but when he returns to his childhood home he finds that he’s often out of reception – something we’ve all experienced from time to time – so his inability to use the phone at critical times is explained without having to resort to something mysterious as the reason. <br /><br />Less understandable is the protagonist’s decision to run through a dense expanse of woodland at a critical time in the novel when he could have used his Landrover. The choice is not explained, but finding the car’s engine to have been tampered with (for example) would’ve provided a sound basis for his decision, fitted well with the narrative, and would not have left this reader wondering ‘Why did he do that?’ instead.<br /><br />There were occasional grammatical lapses, which I thought a little strange for an author of Herbert’s experience. Perhaps they are borne of long habit and survived in the published text because his publisher did not see fit to provide him with an editor. They include the phrase ‘had began’ rather than ‘had begun’, which was repeated throughout the book (examples can be found on pages 214 and 274). Elsewhere, he uses ‘adverse’ for ‘averse’ (p. 411), ‘comprised of’ for ‘composed of’ or simply ‘comprised’, and (frequently) ‘further’ for ‘farther’. That said, his writing is otherwise rich with imagery and description and is a pleasure to read.<br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed this book but I think it could’ve been a lot darker - it was closer to fantasy than to horror.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16323911571047223806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer244517403" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11921619289387324446">Stephen King recommended author as noted in Chapter 9 of Berkley's 1983 paperback edition of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563.Danse_Macabre' title='Danse Macabre by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Danse Macabre</a>.<br/><br/>I've read Herbert before and think he could have done better with this novel. It started out pretty good and I was settled in for a great page-turner, but soon became distracted by all the sex scenes(albeit well-written). <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[And what's with the prepubescent fairy sex.   <span id="freeText11921619289387324446" style="display:none">Stephen King recommended author as noted in Chapter 9 of Berkley's 1983 paperback edition of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563.Danse_Macabre" title="Danse Macabre by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Danse Macabre</a>.<br /><br />I've read Herbert before and think he could have done better with this novel. It started out pretty good and I was settled in for a great page-turner, but soon became distracted by all the sex scenes(albeit well-written). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And what's with the prepubescent fairy sex. His description of this fairy is that of a 13 year old girl with no pubic hair, small breasts, and slight figure. I get this is a fairy, but couldn't she have been more mature-looking. The sex scenes with her just made me feel a bit dirty/creeped-out. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I'm very far from being a prude and am very open-minded, but it didn't seem like most of the sex scenes forwarded the story. There were continuity errors and typos galore, and each time I noticed them it took me out of the story.<br /><br />I really wanted to like this story, it seemed like such a good premise. But it turned out to be predictable, with long-winded and boring descriptions, and stereotyped characters. If this is your first Herbert, please try something else of his before giving up on him. </span>

<div id="review_2103614689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2103614689" />
    <a title="Frank" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7620837-frank"><img alt="Frank" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442852163p2/7620837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2103614689?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frank" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frank" href="/user/show/7620837-frank">Frank</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7620837-frank?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7620837-frank?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2103614689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4716963395007262393">I've read a few other books by Herbert, who is sometimes considered the "Stephen King of Britain", and for the most part they have been enjoyable horror tales. This one was quite a departure from his usual fare. I guess you could call it an adult erotic fairy tale. <br/><br/>The protagonist, Thom Kindred, who is only 27, has had a stroke and needs time to recover. To do this, he goes back to his childhood home of Castle Bracken where he and his mother lived in a nearby cottage called Little Bracken. Durin</span>
  <span id="freeText4716963395007262393" style="display:none">I've read a few other books by Herbert, who is sometimes considered the "Stephen King of Britain", and for the most part they have been enjoyable horror tales. This one was quite a departure from his usual fare. I guess you could call it an adult erotic fairy tale. <br><br>The protagonist, Thom Kindred, who is only 27, has had a stroke and needs time to recover. To do this, he goes back to his childhood home of Castle Bracken where he and his mother lived in a nearby cottage called Little Bracken. During his childhood, his mother told him tales of fairies and other mythical creatures up until her sudden death but she never disclosed who Thom's father was. The master of Castle Bracken paid for Thom's schooling but was it out of kindheartedness or was it for some other reason? Upon Thom's return home, strange happenings start to occur involving elves, witches, fairies, and other creatures who live in the woods around the castle. This included some very erotic sequences that definitely were not written for children! In the end, the tale was a classic good vs. evil story with a clash between the forces of darkness and the goodness of the "faeryfolkis."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504223794ra/23735150.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know this Herbert novel has received some very mixed reviews with some hating it and others loving it. I was kind of in the middle and would mildly recommend it for lovers of fairy tales.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14676440393832498531">This is more of a 2.5 star book, but Goodreads doesn't have half-star ratings for reviewers. That said, while certain horror aspects of 'Once' are more than effective (such as the succubus), too much detracts from that.<br/><br/>First of all, there's far too much fluff involved.   <span id="freeText14676440393832498531" style="display:none">This is more of a 2.5 star book, but Goodreads doesn't have half-star ratings for reviewers. That said, while certain horror aspects of 'Once' are more than effective (such as the succubus), too much detracts from that.<br /><br />First of all, there's far too much fluff involved. I found myself skimming pages of it in attempts to find my way back to the plot. Second, the ending was a bit horrendous if you think about it. Amusingly enough, it can be summarized as 'And then the villain defeats themself, the person everyone thought was dead is perfectly okay, and the main character inherits everything and becomes Jesus.' I'm not kidding about that last part--it was discussed at least twice over the course of the novel. Of course, there are a couple minor things that bugged me, such as the repetition of a few elements from 'The Magic Cottage' that were more annoying than anything. And if I have to hear one more thing about 'juices' of all sorts, I might scream. There is only so many times one can use the exact same description, and that number is decidedly less than what Herbert used.<br /><br />It's not the worst book I've ever read, but it's definitely in the mediocre range.</span>

  <span id="freeText16083081490148930158" style="display:none">Review of Once by James Herbert<br />5 Stars<br /><br />Going in, I sort of expected a horror story, because that is the genre for which Mr. Herbert is so well-known. Instead, I found a very realistic and believable contemporary fairy tale, myth and legend come to vibrant life in the English countryside. Thom Kindred, product of a single mother, was raised till age ten in the cottage called “Little Bracken,” on the estate of Sir Russell Bleeth, whose son was tutored by Thom’s mother. She died when Thom was ten, and Sir Russell paid for his boarding school from then on out. Now at twenty-seven, four months after a stroke, Thom returns to Little Bracken for a time of recuperation. It is also the catalyst for his eyes to be opened, quite literally as well as metaphorically, as he re-discovers the unseen world that lies only a veil apart from our own, the world of Fae. <br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_500384827" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/500384827" />
    <a title="Clare" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16241318-clare"><img alt="Clare" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431856573p2/16241318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/500384827?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clare" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clare" href="/user/show/16241318-clare">Clare</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer500384827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14666559723310130712">Thom returns to his childhood home to convalesce after suffering a horrific accident. The cottage he was brought up in is located in a forest which is part of an estate owned by the Bleeth family. Thom's best friend from childhood is Hugo Bleeth - son of Sir Russell Bleeth the wealthy owner of the estate (who happens to be very ill and on the brink of death). Hugo welcomes his friend back into the fold and introduces him to Nell - an intriguing seductress who has been hired to care for his sick </span>
  <span id="freeText14666559723310130712" style="display:none">Thom returns to his childhood home to convalesce after suffering a horrific accident. The cottage he was brought up in is located in a forest which is part of an estate owned by the Bleeth family. Thom's best friend from childhood is Hugo Bleeth - son of Sir Russell Bleeth the wealthy owner of the estate (who happens to be very ill and on the brink of death). Hugo welcomes his friend back into the fold and introduces him to Nell - an intriguing seductress who has been hired to care for his sick father and who Hugo has asked to help his convalescing friend from time to time. Soon after returning home, Thom realises the forest that he thought he knew so well from childhood is enchanted and home to fairies, elves and every other mythical Enid Blyton type being you can think of. Along with being utterly spellbound by these wonderful creatures, Thom quickly realises that an evil air is also lurking around the estate and he is being drawn into a sinister plan. This is James Herbert's offering of a grown up fairy tale, what with evil goings on and eroticism thrown in for good measure. I found it so difficult to get into this book. Part one - the prelude to the main story - was so over descriptive of things that had no relevance to the actual story and I found myself getting bored by the time I'd found out all about the main character in the first chapter. I kept with it though as this was a James Herbert novel and I've enjoyed everything I've read of his previously. By the time we get to part two, the pace of the book picks up and at last it starts to grab me. We actually get to the meat of the story and this is far, far better than the 200 pages that has preceded it. I actually looked forward to picking up the book to read. In my opinion I think the book could have been condensed into a shorter novel by cutting out the irrelevant stuff along the way. If James Herbert thought he was obliged to stretch the novel to it's 470 pages for the sake of it then I think he was wrong. I remember reading Funhouse written under a pseudonym of Dean Koontz and it was over in about 200 pages: fast paced, absorbing, thrilling. Much better than the drudgery of having to read pages of blurb for the sake of stretching a decent enough story to an acceptable amount of pages. All this aside I do think it would make an excellent film. The plot isn't too thinky and with the fantasy element I reckon it'd be fantastic to watch on the big screen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14666559723310130712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36550957-lou-nixon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2144147393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16717711292934380524">Er...this was a book lent to me by a colleague as I wanted to read something a bit different to what I am used to. First of all-it is very easy to read. Too easy to read, really-with the language and the storylines about magic and fairy's it is like a children's book but with a lot (and I mean a lot!) of needless sex. If you took the sex out of the book, it would seriously be only about 20% of it's actual size. And the sex isn't good.<br/><br/>The book has a very 'teenage boy-with a hard-on' vibe to it. E</span>
  <span id="freeText16717711292934380524" style="display:none">Er...this was a book lent to me by a colleague as I wanted to read something a bit different to what I am used to. First of all-it is very easy to read. Too easy to read, really-with the language and the storylines about magic and fairy's it is like a children's book but with a lot (and I mean a lot!) of needless sex. If you took the sex out of the book, it would seriously be only about 20% of it's actual size. And the sex isn't good.<br /><br />The book has a very 'teenage boy-with a hard-on' vibe to it. Every female character we meet he notices how 'sensual' she she is, he assess her weight, her figure,whether she is wearing a bra-is that some nipple showing through her top? whether she looks at him in a seductive way. it is ridiculous. And I'm not kidding-every. single. female. character in the whole book. There isn't a female character who is not sexualised.<br /><br />And the fairy masturbating in the forest? The fairy that looks like a child (but don't worry folks, actually isn't a child!!). If you are turned on by a person and going through your head is 'she looks like a child.'- whether she is a child or not or whether she just looks exactly like a child-does not matter. It's not ok. and this theme crops up more than once. The fairys 'child-like lack of pubic hair' is a definite focus in the characters brain and this is uncomfortable especially as the overall conclusion to this seems to be- don't worry-it's totally ok because they're not actually children. Being turned on by women who look like children because they look like children is not ok, especially in this sort of silly magical story that, other-wise feels a bit like an extended nursery rhyme.<br /><br />Sex aside, it's still not good. Not a lot happens-monsters can't just be monsters, they have to be penis sucking monsters. It's all just a bit too cringe and cliched for me. I knew that Thom's mum was a fairy very early on. Of course she is. And I knew that he would be related to the Bleeth family-how cliched can you get? The storyline lacked any real imagination as if he just wanted some flimsy storyline to go between his gratuitous sex scenes. I almost feel like this is a joke-book that was written by the author to see how stupid his audience is and people just haven't realised it.<br /><br />Anyway. Didn't like this book. Can you tell?</span>

<div id="review_218095713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218095713" />
    <a title="Sophia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5180153-sophia"><img alt="Sophia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319039181p2/5180153.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218095713?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia" href="/user/show/5180153-sophia">Sophia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218095713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2815498701465973552">Once was completely bonkers, but also utterly compelling. I'm still not sure whether I thought it was terrible or brilliant - I may take a few days to mull it over and work out which.<br/><br/>The story follows Thom Kindred, a 27-year-old man who has suffered a stroke which has left him with a weakness down his left side. After being discharged from hospital, he returns to his childhood home deep in the Shropshire countryside to convalesce. The cottage in the woods, part of the estate belonging to his bes</span>
  <span id="freeText2815498701465973552" style="display:none">Once was completely bonkers, but also utterly compelling. I'm still not sure whether I thought it was terrible or brilliant - I may take a few days to mull it over and work out which.<br /><br />The story follows Thom Kindred, a 27-year-old man who has suffered a stroke which has left him with a weakness down his left side. After being discharged from hospital, he returns to his childhood home deep in the Shropshire countryside to convalesce. The cottage in the woods, part of the estate belonging to his best friend's father, is of a strange design, but Thom remembers being happy there as a child, before his mother committed suicide in the nearby lake. <br /><br />Thom's friend, Hugo, lives up at the big house - Castle Bracken - with his dying father and a creepy servant whose nickname is Bones. When I tell you that the book's climax takes place there (during a thunderstorm and power outage, no less), you'll soon realise that this novel is not entirely free of horror cliche. But it's not the creepy castle that tests the reader's credibility... it's some of the novel's more "unusual" characters.<br /><br />Once is populated with a cast of elves, fairies, pixies, brownies, mud-monsters, sentient animals and a humpbacked succubus (who in one memorable scene was chasing our hero round the kitchen table, trying to snatch a jar of sperm, while being dive-bombed by fairies emerging from a book and hit by a broom wielded by an angry pixie). Yes, I did say sperm; there's a LOT of sex in this book - much of it of the toe-curling squirmy eewww variety. It took an awful lot of effort and determination to suspend my disbelief enough to get through this book.<br /><br />But even when writing nonsense like this, James Herbert is still a fantastic author, and manages to make it all really exciting. There's a scene involving spiders that's as good as anything he's ever written, and the ending - though horribly cliched - was so riveting that I couldn't help staying up until 2.30 this morning to finish it.<br /><br />I've read a lot of James Herbert books over the years, most of them while I was still in my teens, and this is without doubt the silliest and most incredible of them all. I did enjoy it though, in a self-conscious, half-embarrassed kind of way</span>
  <a data-text-id="2815498701465973552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1409005983" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409005983" />
    <a title="Blaze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1729087-blaze"><img alt="Blaze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576792978p2/1729087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409005983?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blaze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blaze" href="/user/show/1729087-blaze">Blaze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765302854" href="/book/show/1409662.Once">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">nobody ever</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409005983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1057474328543107231">Oh boy, was this book horrendous. <br/>I had such high hopes and I really did try to like it. <i>I wanted</i> to like it. But. It. Was. <i>Horrible!</i><br/>I’m still astounded I didn’t give up midway… and immensely sorry that I didn’t. I should have ditched it.<br/><br/>It was supposed to be a horror/thriller with fae lore (written by a best-selling author no less), but it was actually an extremely badly written, long-winded romance/wannabe “horror” with cookie-cutter characters, bad plot, and some terrible sex scenes thrown in</span>
  <span id="freeText1057474328543107231" style="display:none">Oh boy, was this book horrendous. <br />I had such high hopes and I really did try to like it. <i>I wanted</i> to like it. But. It. Was. <i>Horrible!</i><br />I’m still astounded I didn’t give up midway… and immensely sorry that I didn’t. I should have ditched it.<br /><br />It was supposed to be a horror/thriller with fae lore (written by a best-selling author no less), but it was actually an extremely badly written, long-winded romance/wannabe “horror” with cookie-cutter characters, bad plot, and some terrible sex scenes thrown in for good measure.<br /><br />This book had fairies in it and took place in a fucking magical forest - the prose was supposed to be dark and enchanting! Instead it was almost as stiff as the dialogue, occasionally eye-roll worthy, and sometimes read like something plucked out of a boring manual. And the word choice was so weird at times. The sentence <i>"she smeared her breasts over his chest"</i> is an actual thing that exists in this book. I mean... did she use a butter-knife or what?<br /><br />And don’t even get me started on the way the women were depicted and treated in this sorry excuse for a novel! All the women in this waste of paper were the embodiment of two of the most overused and annoying archetypes for female characters - the evil seductress and the innocent (but still very sexual) child-like woman who in this case exists only because the author needed someone to infodump lore, support the hero emotionally, and provide him with something to stare at open-mouthed. <br /><br />Which brings us to the protagonist. He was, to put it in one word, <i>bland</i>. And dense. But mostly bland. His ability to have the obvious (and logical) pointed out to him but still deny it was astonishing. Buddy, you just walked through a forest full of fairy creatures - why the hell is the existence of a witch so hard to wrap your head around?!<br />As for the antagonists... cliché, underdeveloped, and disappointing. The same goes for the anticlimactic ending of this piece of trash.<br /><br />I just can't with this book. I don't know why it made me so angry but it... it's just bad. I could rant for hours.<br />It bored me to tears and pissed me off at the same time. The only thing it's good for is to decorate my bookshelf because the hardback has a misleadingly pretty cover.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1057474328543107231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_25425816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25425816" />
    <a title="Rosie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1269587-rosie"><img alt="Rosie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590708063p2/1269587.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
